I'm a new player who has avoided tank because of the responsibility (yet I'm SUPPORT?!), but here's a lot of my thoughts.   1A) I don't think his Block should even be an ability but rather a feature of Nemesis form when he's not using Pummel. This way he's more vulnerable (but has mobility) while using Pummel, and then if the player chooses to stop engaging then his movement will be slowed down while also taking less damage. The damage reduction decreases gradually until it reaches zero and forces him to Pummel once again in order to be effective in the fight. With that block FEATURE he's able to survive a little longer until he gets backup since the only way to kill him while he's not Pummeling is his back hitbox, which only someone who is skilled enough could target before he turns around to Pummel them.   1B) Nemesis while not in ult doesn't even last that long for Block as an ability to be a reasonable use of that time (and again therefore shouldn't be an ability but a feature like I mentioned). With what I proposed in 1a, maybe Nemesis SHOULD be a toggle. Hear me out, THAT'S setting an actual tempo. Maybe his punches take a little longer in-between and/or he does less damage with each punch in order for such a toggle to not be ridiculous, but I'd prefer he have the two playstyles than what's going on for him right now since him regaining armor every Nemesis basically undoes the damage done to him. Even with the toggle he won't be Doom in the backline, but he'd ACTUALLY be able to a lil something something?? YES please! It should be noted he won't be able to switch to his regular form during Annihilation, but until that key is pressed the player gets to choose from moment to moment how they want to play it.  2) Even if it becomes a feature instead, Ramattra shouldn't be able to block during his ult. That combo is a boring way to play. He's already doing damage endlessly in an AOE to enemies within that range after pressing just ONE key, so he shouldn't have THAT strong of a defense. Sure Annihilation's damage is over time and using Pummel during ult does something to ensure kills, but literally continuing to do damage rather passively while in a defensive stance so you don't die as quickly sounds so uninteresting. Right now, the person at his back better be LUCKY enough to be damage or tank in order to hit his hitbox quickly enough to end the ult before the whole team dies. Imagine instead if the whole team manages to target him even while the nanites are draining them, in which case he should die along with the couple of ally squishies who were unfortunate. If more health (preferred over additional armor) during Annihilation would be needed for that, I wouldn't be mad at it because of the actual skill involved in killing him or even just evading him.   3) Does Annihilation really NOT have damage falloff? I get its reach is 15m but come on, change that because someone backing out will still be hit the same amount when to me it makes more sense that the nanites be more concentrated the closer you are to Ramattra.  4) In keeping with Pummel piercing shields, perhaps the nanites from Annihilation are surely unable to reach enemies through shields and barriers but instead of being stopped completely the nanites will target those first to break them, and then resume killing leftover enemies. That way, if the team does not manage to run away or kill him by then they're essentially facing a reset because of lack or coordination, etc. If the team still manages to die en masse after the amount of time it takes for the bubble to either break or expire, it would be classified as a skill issue.

This is the other negative side of putting heroes in the battle pass that I've mentioned before. They run the risk of not only making the character overperform, but also underperform on arrival. Imagine being a dev trying to cautiously balance a hero to not cause outrage that this new hero is "meta" and has to be unlocked or bought through the battlepass just for your team to perform well, while also being good enough that they don't feel underwhelming. That's an impossible position to put your developers in. I actually think its better for the game for heroes to overperform on release rather than underperform. Nothing is worse than a new hero who is dead on arrival and drives no interest.

I mean, its relatively analogous to "making space" in a lot of ways and Ram just doesn't do it. How do any of his abilities outside of his ult control the pace/balance of the match? Sure his ult does, but isn't that true for 80% of the cast?

Buff Idea: Remove the movement speed penalty for his Block.  Like Flats said, there is very little benefit to Block due to how slow it makes you. Enemies can easily get away from Ramattra's short range during the block or completely surround Ramattra by the time Nemesis wears off. However, without the movement speed penalty, Block becomes far more useful and fun. It can be used to help close the distance or escape a fight without taking as much damage, and it lets players alternate between punching enemies and protecting themselves without possibly losing their targets.

as silly as it might sound, I think the appeal of ramatra is that he is trying to be a jack of all trades, right? Like, in theory he can poke, cut sightlines, brawl, zone, and both sustain and burst damage all depending on how aggressive he's played between his two forms.  because of this, I think the buff to ramatra shouldn't be a numbers buff, (although I think it is silly that his snare doesn't actually snare, make it make sense lol) but instead he just needs the rest of the puzzle pieces, that being a small self heal and a mobility gimmick.   I propose: a hanzo-like double jump and *and maybe a wall climb*in nemesis form, and a small heal over time whilst in non-nemesis form, maybe in the form of shield health instead of regular health like zenyatta/sigma. I actually like the numbers on him at a glance, but it's clear that he's going to be really punished for brawling, which eliminates pretty much half of his kit *until* it's time to ult. I think that having mobility whilst in brawl mode will help him commit to actually brawling, as a lot of the time it's very easy to get displaced away from a fight with all the tanks and super high mobility everybody seems to have. He has no value against anybody who can get away, which is like 90% of the game, so going all in to his "jack of all trades" appeal by letting him chase/escape out of a brawl and return to poking just makes way more sense to me from a design standpoint. Honestly, I think I'd prefer if Blizz decided to release a character slightly underpowered rather then OP, especially if that character is tied to the battlepass. If they intentionally aim for slightly under powered with a few buffs in mind then they can see how he performs and what people want out of him first, and release those buffs to make those better. Like if people want him to be a good Anti-Air tank, then they could buff the height of his pull, how much it pulls, or if it negates movement abilities entirely. If players want him to be more of a toolbox tank, then making his ability to switch forms have a few second cooldown but he can stay in either form for as long as possible would let him get maximum value out of that forms abilities. Underpowered characters with room to grow means that the devs can look at where specifically he's lacking and buff him up, rather then look at an OP character and figure out how to nerf it without ruining the characters playability. It also means they if they underestimate how strong a character is, then that underestimate is still closer aligned to the rest of the cast instead of far and away better like Sojourn.  It also feels better across the board, since a character who's OP and dominates the meta isn't great for the health of the game and nerfing it sucks for any players who enjoy playing the character. Instead, releasing a weaker character and then bringing them up to par with the rest means no waiting for 2 - 4 weeks with a bad metagame centered on this character before a patch rolls out and anyone who plays the character will be happy to receive a buff. I look at it kinda like how Blizzard implemented their reduced XP system into WOW. At first your character would recieve less XP after playing for so long as a debuff, which was largely hated. Instead it was flipped to be a positive thing, where you'd receive an XP boost if your character was "rested" after not playing so long, and this would wear off. Even though the numbers were exactly the same, making it a positive thing that helps the players made it feel good. So, making Ramattra slightly weaker and then bringing him up is better for the health of the game rather then making him oppresively OP.  It also helps reduce pay to win accusations against the battlepass if the tied in character is weaker. Especially since by the time a balance patch to buff him up rolls around many people may be close to unlocking him for free just by playing anyway. Personally I think this could be a good design concept moving forward, rather then splashing in with a new OP hero and then trying to balance that hero later down the line.

That way, those abilities can afford to be a tiny bit weaker. Although I am disgusted by his block, why does his block (and DF block for that matter) not block the total incoming damage? I mean I guess for DF you want to incentivize opponents to shoot you so you can charge your gauntlet but charging your gauntlet fully should heal the damage that you've taken from it so it's actually rewarding. For Ramattra, his block does nothing. Maybe blocking damage should be the thing that could maintain up time of his hulk form? That way the 50% reduction is worth it, and opponents are incentivized not to shoot you? I dunno - I'm fine with shields blocking his ult but I think if they do, his ult should "focus" on them and concentrate damage onto the shields. What I think might be the intention for Ramattra's vortex is largely going to be prediction-based. A PhaMercy is typically high up, yes, but should Mercy be run in any other instance (and lets face it, the Devs in the upper ranks are few and far between) the intention may be to catch Mercy as she's using GA to zip around between team mates, as not everyone would be up in the air. A very unlikely scenario, but that's the only way I could see such a short height on that ability having any real value. Catching people off of cooldowns when they don't have their mobility options and the stray "straggler Mercy", basically is what it seems like it may get limited to in terms of use.  The slowdown can help a bit, perhaps with a Widow on the backline to line up shots a little easier -- but it doesn't seem to be as strong of a slowdown as it was in the video, so it'd require a touch of coordination to take advantage of the small slowdown window it could provide.  Additionally: They need to remove the ult cancel ability. It makes no sense outside of "BE CAREFUL WHEN USING THIS CHARACTERS ULT PLZ".  tl;dr: Looks fun to play.
